<review>What a pleasant experience we had at this resort, after a long day at the slopes, all we hoped for was a warm place to lay our heads down since we decided to stay the night in big bear, this spot beyond exceeded our expectations,  the place was nice and neat,  everything so clean and tighty,  the atmosphere of these cabin like houses are very cozy and accommodated the climate just right, we recommend this place and we will definitely be returning for our future stays, did I mention that their bigger cottages have their private  small jacuzzi, it accommodates 2-3 people comfortably. <Review>Better than we expected! Impressed! Great location next to food, liquor and park to sled (Must buy day parking pass $5 at liquor store and other stores, places) as well as Alpine Slide Park. Staying in 2 story cabin, two queens and sofa bed. Comes with kitchen, fridge, pots and pans fireplace, everything you need. NO bed bugs, prior review scared me and I checked throughly. No bugs, no sign of bugs faces, stains and no bites. Store stocked with surprisingly reasonable prices on items. Extremely nice and helpful staff. Also close to Boulder Bay. I'd like to suggest a hand rail on the left side of staircase to go up the stairs for support. Other than that extremely pleased.<//Review>< name>

< Review>
Resort is conveniently located. Was responsible price. Had a cute kitchen and sitting area. Check in was super easy with everything texted. It worked out great. There are a few things to be aware of. Our cabin backed up to the main road. Which made sleeping difficult with the constant lights and loud noises. The mattresses had a memory foam topper but I found the beds to be uncomfortable. The ac unit was great and loud to help block a lot of noise but it sucks up everything from outside and when we arrived it smelled like someone had just smoked a cigar in our unit. There is no bathtub, so with a toddler and baby that was hard. We ended up staying one night. If your looking for a quick place to crash to ski. Awesome. But if you have kids don't stay in cabin 20. Too much noise.</Review>

< Text>
My honey surprised me and brought me here for my birthday.

It's easy to see from the road and they maintain the grounds very well. All of the cabins have icicle lights that are a nice touch. There is also plenty of parking and the parkingnlot is spacious.

The cabin that we stayed in was quite small but cozy.

The pros
The heater worked great and keeps every part of the cabin warm.

There is a mini kitchen with a nice size stove and sink

The bed was comfortable

Rooms are clean for the most part

Water pressure in the shower was good

The person at the desk was friendly

The cons
You can hear everything your neighbors are saying and seeing on tv. We had noisy neighbors who had on loud music and heard their conversations.

The TV in the room is really small

The sofa was not comfortable.  It was pretty hard.

The shower is tiny and the shower head is short.

There is a small and old microwave in the kitchenette

Probably won't be staying here again at the price we paid.<//Text>

<name>Rich W< /name>< text>
It's a good value and my experience was what I expected it to be from an older facility like most of the cabins in Big Bear. Included with that is old furniture, old kitchenware and old typical old cabin accoutrements like sticky doors, windows that could use a little lubrication and typical creaks and cracks that most people might find is par for the course.

The location is good with a liquor store with groceries across the street and some restaurants in quick walking distance but parking can be challenging on a busy week.

They do supply low bandwidth wifi access and satellite tv but air conditioning is not available. It does get a little stuffy on hot days. Central room heater works.

My only real criticism is management doesn't limit pool activities so beware of loud activities near the facility pool late at night for cabins adjacent the pool.<//text>

<review>I had reserved cabin number 8 several months in advance for a romantic holiday-weekend getaway. This cabin was advertised to have a private whirlpool, fenced yard, full kitchen, fireplace, and no shared walls. We bought our firewood in advance, took time off work, and made the trip a day early to stay in a hotel at the bottom of the mountain the night before. We wanted to get an earlier start the next morning, as heavy traffic was expected. Once we arrived at Bear Creek, we were impressed with the size and cleanliness of the facility. The little office store even had free material to use as firestarters. We checked in, received our cabin key, and made our way to cabin 6. Wait, 6? We paid extra for cabin 8. Heading back to the office, they advised us they had given someone else cabin 8 and reassigned us to 6. This was a smaller cabin, no fireplace, no private yard, no whirlpool. The office was then so nice to let us know that "Oh, the whirlpool hasn't even worked in over a year. We don't charge extra for that anyway". <username>James Churchman<//username>< Review>
This place was awesome. I'm an old man who spent a lot of time in my younger years up here so my daughter took me on a spontaneous visit. She just happened across it on her phone while up there and we popped in. There was no one in the office when we arrived but it was past 5 maybe even 6, they had a number to call and someone showed up shortly. I think her name was Heather and she was very sweet and accommodating. I understand that's usually how mountain places like this goes, some of the workers live onsite or close by so even if they aren't in the office, they are close by, so don't let that detur you.
Each "room" is actually its own little cabin home. We asked for a 2 bed so it had a living room (with real wood burning fire place, futon couch and tv), its own kitchen (stove, oven, microwave, full fridge, coffee pot, toaster and dishes) a bedroom (ours had 2 queen beds) and of course a bathroom. They also have bbqs outside, every other cabin. They accepted our dogs which was a huge plus. They have a pool but it was too cold to swim. They do require you to buy wood from them for the fireplace ($7 a bundle) no outside wood. It was so nice and relaxing we just kept staying for a few nights. Really a great place and am glad we found it, hope to go back soon. Again, the manager or lady in charge while we were there (Heather) was amazingly kind and accommodating, she was a huge part of making the stay so wonderful, thank you!!< /Review>

<Text>We found ourselves in need of a veterinarian after realizing our cat had a serious injury that we hadn't noticed. I called the hospital to get an estimate of the cost and the respondent was calm, kind, and able to provide me with valuable information regarding what options might be taken to address the injury and what they would cost. We were able to get an estimate and schedule an appointment for later that day, and met with one of the newer veterinary doctors.

Highlights of our visitation:
- Great people skills on behalf of staff, were able to reassure us about options and ways to manage injury while acknowledging seriousness and possibilities resulting from wounds. They were able to calm us, but did not attempt to falsely reassure us. They were respectful and professional.
- Frank discussion over options available to treat injuries, the associating costs, and the pros and cons of each.Treated us as active participants in how they could and would like to treat the patient.
- Pointed out additional problems and issues unnoticed at the time (medication updates, mild parasitic infection) and was able to incorporate those into the course of treatment.
- In case it seems like I'm putting too much emphasis on the doctoral staff, the logistics staff was excellent in tracking and assisting us with the necessary information needed to make an appointment and follow up appointments.
- They healed our cat. They got a little animal whose main way of communicating an unnoticed injury was "be quieter and move around less" and helped fix them and let us know how to help fix them so they'd be living a better life and wouldn't be in pain. And then they did it again with the 5+ dog owners that came in after us. That takes skill, heart, and guts.

Thus, five stars. It's not for everyone - it costs something, and we got off lucky with what we needed to pay for. Not everyone is in our financial situation. We were lucky. If you love your pet though, and you're willing to do what needs to be done to help it even if it might be painful or anxious for you, I would look here.</Text>< GmapID>

< text>
This is my 1st traveling placement. I was working with a recruiter who unexpectedly left the company 1 month after my placement started and was quickly followed up by Megan who filled me in on the situation and has been communicative, informative, and transparent thus far.

The 1st recruiter was very attentive to my needs and prior to me agreeing to work with PHS followed up with me well and generally continued to maintain communication throughout. I have been paid on time so far and am happy with being paid weekly.

I will say that when filling out documents, the recruiter seemed to not know the purpose of some documents..however, which could have resulted in me not getting my medical/dental/vision benefits (good thing I clarified!). When I asked questions about documents though..he was quick to follow up with more knowledgable workers if he was unsure about answers to my questions. He definitely took the time to answer my questions and was attentive.

I did have 1 questionable experience with this recruiter regarding how certain fees would be covered (license, medical requirements to work, etc). He said that PHS would cover these fees as long as I sent receipts, when in the end, he meant that these fees would be taken out of my paycheck by the hourly rather than an upfront fee.

Overall..my experience has been mostly good so far.</text>
